Brian Heater
Hardware Editor


Brian Heater is the Hardware Editor at TechCrunch. He worked for a number of leading tech publications, including Engadget, PCMag, Laptop, and Tech Times, where he served as the Managing Editor. His writing has appeared in Spin, Wired, Playboy, Entertainment Weekly, The Onion, Boing Boing, Publishers Weekly, The Daily Beast and various other publications. He hosts the weekly Boing Boing interview podcast RiYL, has appeared as a regular NPR contributor and shares his Queens apartment with a rabbit named Lucy.

Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2281426,"date":"2022-03-08T10:11:21","date_gmt":"2022-03-08T18:11:21","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281426"},"modified":"2022-03-08T12:53:17","modified_gmt":"2022-03-08T20:53:17","slug":"the-iphone-se-returns","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/the-iphone-se-returns\/","title":{"rendered":"The iPhone SE returns for $429"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Two years after reviving the line, Apple\u2019s bringing the SE back for another go. The iPhone\u2019s little sibling won support when it was unveiled in 2018 as a low-cost alternative to the flagship smartphone. The line is a way of keeping the iOS software fresh, while maintaining lower price points through older designs and some last-gen components.<\/p>\n<p>For those who\u2019ve lost the Apple design thread post-iPhone X, it\u2019s a welcome way to maintain a more classic design. And, perhaps most importantly, it\u2019s a way to stay in the Apple ecosystem in an age when flagships routinely top $1,000. The new handset arrives with an upgraded chip &#8212; the A15 bionic, the same chip found on the company&#8217;s latest flagship, iPhone 13. That&#8217;s coupled with the arrival of 5G, bringing the latest cellular technology to the entire line.<\/p>\n<p>As expected, the new version of the budget device sticks to the old glass and aluminum design, built around a 4.7-inch Retina HD display (a decided downgrade from the iPhone 13). The device is IP67 water resistant and &#8212; perhaps most notably &#8212; retains its Touch ID button, which has been long gone from the premium Face ID-sporting devices. The battery has been improved over the last model, though it&#8217;s not entirely clear whether that&#8217;s an upgrade in capacity or simply a result of the new chip.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281426\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281509\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281509\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2281509\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg\" alt=\"A15 Bionic\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg 1554w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg?resize=680,382 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-a15-bionic.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281509\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The camera gets upgraded with a 12-megapixel lens, coupled with a number of computational photography upgrades that come along with that new chip. That includes improved skin tone shots and reduced noise in photos. Like the battery, this is likely more a direct result of the new chip versus any major hardware upgrade.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2281536\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2281536\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2281536\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"630\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg 1734w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg?resize=150,92 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg?resize=300,184 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg?resize=768,472 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg?resize=680,418 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg?resize=1536,944 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-08-at-1.20.09-PM.jpg?resize=50,31 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2281536\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Software is a big reason to buy the new phone, versus just going with a similarly specced old unit. As such, the company notes that the new device will continue to get iOS updates for &#8220;years to come.&#8221; The handset is still easily the cheapest in the iPhone family, though it gets a bump over the $399 of the last generation. This one starts at a (still reasonable) $429. It goes up for preorder this Friday and will hit stores March 18.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/apple-march-2022-event\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-event-banner1.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about the Apple March 2022 event on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Two years after reviving the line, Apple\u2019s bringing the SE back for another go. The iPhone\u2019s little sibling won support when it was unveiled in 2018 as a low-cost alternative to the flagship smartphone. from Apple\u2019s Peek Performance event"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">CES is done. MWC has come and gone. That means it&#8217;s time for <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/apples-next-event-is-march-8\/\">another Apple event<\/a>. The company sent out invites for its Peek [sic] Performance event last week. These things sure have a way of sneaking up on you now that everything\u2019s gone virtual. The event kicks off today at <strong>10AM PT\/1PM ET<\/strong>. Follow along right here to get the news as it happens.<\/p>\n<p>There\u2019s been a steady trickle of leaks leading up to today\u2019s event. Though it\u2019s been notably absent of any major bombshells. Don\u2019t expect to see, say, the iPhone 14 or Apple Watch 8. Stranger things have happened, of course, but neither of those products are due for a major refresh.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"bLKeoEtZEi\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/what-we-expect-from-apples-peek-performance-event\/\">What we expect from Apple\u2019s Peek Performance event<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2280816\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;What we expect from Apple\u2019s Peek Performance event&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/what-we-expect-from-apples-peek-performance-event\/embed\/#?secret=Sfjw9MEUAe#?secret=bLKeoEtZEi\" data-secret=\"bLKeoEtZEi\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>Instead, we\u2019re expect updates to some of Apple&#8217;s more unsung product lines, with the on-again-off-again iPhone SE taking center stage. The budget handset is overdue for an update, and the SE 3 is expected to arrive with a similar classic-style iPhone design, 5G and, potentially, Face ID. This may also end up becoming an iPad event, with Apple refreshing the tablet line, including a new Pro, Air and standard iPad.<\/p>\n<p>Other rumors include a new Mac Mini and upgrades to the iMac, MacBook Air and Mac Pro lines, as well as an external Apple display that costs an arm, but not a leg.<\/p>\n<p>Bookmark this link to follow along live. performance","slug":"peek-performance","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576991938"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576991938"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576991938"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576991938"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576991938"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2281383,"date":"2022-03-08T08:09:14","date_gmt":"2022-03-08T16:09:14","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2281383"},"modified":"2022-03-08T08:31:31","modified_gmt":"2022-03-08T16:31:31","slug":"ges-worm-robot-sports-roach-style-whiskers-to-remove-fat-deposits-from-sewage-pipes","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/08\/ges-worm-robot-sports-roach-style-whiskers-to-remove-fat-deposits-from-sewage-pipes\/","title":{"rendered":"GE\u2019s worm robot sports roach-style whiskers to remove fat deposits from sewage pipes"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">When we talk about the three Ds of automation, the dull and dangerous bits are generally understood. Robotics can play a key role in getting humans out of harm&#8217;s way and replacing extremely boring, repetitive work. But what about the dirty part? As far as headlines go, I don\u2019t know that I\u2019ve written one that better fits the middle D.<\/p>\n<p>Snake robotics are nothing new, of course. It\u2019s a clever form factor capable of making tight squeezes that would be otherwise impossible for more conventional systems. Carnegie Mellon University, for one, has been developing them for a long time, as has NASA. This giant earthworm robot, meanwhile, actually started life as part of DARPA\u2019s Underminer program designed to develop tunneling operations for the military.<\/p>\n<p>Now under the GE umbrella, the robot carries the name Pipe-worm (Programmable Worm for Irregular Pipeline Exploration). It combines fluid-powered muscles with a system of cockroach-inspired whiskers that help it navigate through pipes. Using tactile feedback, it\u2019s able to determine things like pipe diameter, joints and turns.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281383\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span class=\"embed-youtube embed breakout embed--video\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\"><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/embed\/NmJIuns9nRk?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation\"><\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The robot was recently deployed at a GE research location, navigating through pipes without a significant impact on operations.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThis AI-enabled autonomous robot has the ability to inspect and potentially repair pipelines all on its own, breaking up the formation of solid waste masses like fatbergs that are an ongoing issue with many of our nation\u2019s sewer systems,\u201d says GE robot researcher Deepak Trivedi in <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ge.com\/research\/newsroom\/fatbergs-beware-ge-research-demonstrates-autonomous-pipe-worm-robot-can-demolish-hard\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a release<\/a>. \u201cWe\u2019ve added cockroach-like whiskers to its body that gives it greatly enhanced levels of perception to make sharp turns or negotiate its way through dark, unknown portions of a pipeline network.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The company believes the robot could be deployed for all manner of subterranean inspection, from power plants to fiber optic cables.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>When we talk about the three Ds of automation, the dull and dangerous bits are generally understood. Robotics can play a key role in getting humans out of harm&#8217;s way and replacing extremely boring, repetitive work. But what about the dirty part? As far as headlines go, I don\u2019t know that I\u2019ve written one that acqui-hires team from robotic strawberry-picking startup, Strio.AI"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Amazon-owned robotaxi firm Zoox <a href=\"https:\/\/zoox.com\/journal\/strio-ai-joins-zoox\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">this week announced<\/a> that it has acquired Strio.AI. The Boston-based robotics startup was founded in 2020 by MIT alumns to bring autonomous picking and pruning to strawberry crops. It got up and running quickly during the pandemic, bringing its first prototype system to farms in California and Florida within about six months.<\/p>\n<p>The acquisition is more of an acqui-hire, really. Strio co-founder and CEO Ruijie He joins Zoox as director of Perception, while four of its senior engineers will be integrated into the team. The move also finds the Bay Area-based Zoox opening its first East Coast R&amp;D site with the Strio team.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cDuring our conversations with RJ and the other members of the Strio.AI team, we were continually impressed by their technical expertise, entrepreneurial spirit, and approach to developing state-of-the-art perception systems,\u201d Zoox said in a blog post. \u201cWe\u2019re thrilled to welcome them aboard as we continue advancing our autonomous technology.\u201d<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2281117\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The acquisition means that Strio will be winding down its ag tech work, instead integrating their work in things like perception into Zoox\u2019s broader robotaxi plans. The move comes a few weeks after <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/16\/following-acquisition-by-bowery-traptics-strawberry-picking-robotics-move-into-vertical-farming\/\">Bowery Farming acquired Traptic\u2019s strawberry-picking robots<\/a> for integration into its indoor vertical farms. Like the Zoox move, Bowery\u2019s acquisition effectively took Traptic\u2019s robots out of the field.<\/p>\n<p>Conventional wisdom holds that there\u2019s a lot of opportunity for autonomous robotics in ag tech, but many of the main players in the category have had difficulty making it too far down that road. Abundant\u2019s apple-picking robots are another key example. Though for the robotics category in general, acquisition is often a solid outcome, particularly for a young company like Strio.<\/p>\n<p>For Zoox, meanwhile, it means access to more talent and a presence in the robotics research hub of Boston.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"4l70LaveR4\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/02\/abundants-new-owner-looks-to-revive-the-apple-picking-robot-through-equity-crowdfunding\/\">Abundant\u2019s new owner looks to revive the apple-picking robot through equity crowdfunding<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Abundant\u2019s new owner looks to revive the apple-picking robot through equity crowdfunding&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/02\/abundants-new-owner-looks-to-revive-the-apple-picking-robot-through-equity-crowdfunding\/embed\/#?secret=CSFssMi1xg#?secret=4l70LaveR4\" data-secret=\"4l70LaveR4\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Amazon-owned robotaxi firm Zoox this week announced that it has acquired Strio.AI. The Boston-based robotics startup was founded in 2020 by MIT alumns to bring autonomous picking and pruning to strawberry crops. It got up and running quickly during the pandemic, bringing its first prototype system to farms in California and Florida within about six we expect from Apple\u2019s Peek Performance event"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">The thing about<\/span> these virtual events is they\u2019ve really got a way of sneaking up on you. Back in the good &#8216;ol days of corporate travel, you could expect a few weeks\u2019 heads-up ahead of the big show to allow you the proper time to book a night at the Palo Alto Travelodge (decent Wi-Fi, less decent free breakfast). The move to virtual also means a company doesn\u2019t have to promise you the stars to justify making you sit in front of your computer for an hour.<\/p>\n<p>A steady trickle of leaks have been arriving in recent weeks, pointing to what\u2019s likely to be one of the year\u2019s lower-key events for the company. This is bolstered by the standard release cadence. Apple jammed a lot into its fall event last year &#8212; like, a lot, a lot. We got the iPhone 13, Apple Watch 7, iOS and a couple of iPads that really stole the show. Chip delays and holidays lined up perfectly for one of the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/14\/heres-everything-apple-announced-at-its-event-this-morning\/\">biggest Apple events in recent memory<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1978374\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1978374\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1978374\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"787\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png 2996w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png?resize=150,115 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png?resize=300,231 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png?resize=768,590 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png?resize=680,522 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png?resize=1536,1180 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png?resize=2048,1574 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2020\/04\/Screen-Shot-2020-04-22-at-5.52.08-AM.png?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1978374\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2280965\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>So, no iPhone 14 or Watch 8 <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/apples-next-event-is-march-8\/\">this week<\/a> &#8212; but we may still be getting a new phone, nonetheless. It\u2019s hard to say the company is overdue to launch a new iPhone SE, because the budget handset has had, at best, an irregular schedule. This would be the third-gen SE, following releases in 2016 and 2020. The budget handset (the last gen started at $399) has earned its fans over the years, including our own Devin Coldewey, who <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/09\/14\/the-iphone-se-was-the-best-phone-apple-ever-made-and-now-its-dead\/\">mourned the product\u2019s \u201cdeath\u201d<\/a> the first time around.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Some predictions for the coming new iPhone SE:<br \/>1. Mass production in Mar&#39;22.<br \/>2. Estimated shipments of 25-30 mn units in 2022.<br \/>3. Storage: 64\/128\/256GB.<br \/>4. A15 &amp; 5G support (mmW &amp; Sub-6 GHz).<br \/>5. Casing: white, black, and red.<br \/>6. Similar form factor design to current SE.<\/p>\n<p>&mdash; \u90ed\u660e\u9324 (Ming-Chi Kuo) (@mingchikuo) <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/mingchikuo\/status\/1499721483907907586?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">March 4, 2022<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https:\/\/platform.twitter.com\/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"><\/script><\/div>\n<p>The line is notable for, among other things, serving as the last vestige for Apple\u2019s older industrial design, before iPhones became all screen and notch. Perennial Apple predictor Ming-Chi Kuo was among the first to note the device\u2019s return after a two-year hiatus. The report notes a largely unchanged design, an A15 chip and storage ranging from 64 to 256GB. The star of the show, however, is the addition of 5G on the entry-level device.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>IPads may once again end up stealing the show. A fifth-gen Air is expected, taking a number of cues from last year\u2019s Mini. Like the iPhone SE, the model hasn\u2019t had an upgrade since 2020. Rumors here include optional 5G, the A15 chip and upgraded camera hardware and software.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1739398\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1739398\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1739398\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"682\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg 2000w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2018\/10\/3Q5A5691.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1739398\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> TechCrunch<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Last year offered a pair of super-charged riffs on 2020\u2019s M1 chip, and it seems likely we\u2019ll see the M2 land at some point this year (is this the titular performance we\u2019ll be getting a peek at?). If Apple does announce a new chip, it will almost certainly arrive alongside <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/newsletters\/2022-03-06\/apple-aapl-peek-performance-march-8-event-5g-iphone-se-ipad-air-mac-updates-l0fdz98z\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">some new Mac hardware<\/a>. Leading the pack of rumors this year is a new version of the perennial favorite thin and light MacBook Air. A Mac Mini is also said to be on offer, along with larger, more Pro-like iMacs.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1922941\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1922941\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-1922941\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/pro-display-xdr.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"656\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/pro-display-xdr.png 1095w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/pro-display-xdr.png?resize=150,96 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/pro-display-xdr.png?resize=300,192 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/pro-display-xdr.png?resize=768,492 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/pro-display-xdr.png?resize=680,435 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/12\/pro-display-xdr.png?resize=50,32 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-1922941\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Apple<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The latest rumor to hit the pile is a 27-inch Apple display &#8212; one that lowers the barrier a bit from the 32-inch Pro Display XDR the company currently sells. Apple\u2019s no doubt seen an uptick in demand for such products as much of the world moved to remote work over the past couple of years, but $5,000 was almost certainly too rich for most folks\u2019 blood.<\/p>\n<p>Lastly, these hardware events always arrive with some OS updates in tow. Expect updates for the latest versions of macOS, iOS and iPadOS.<\/p>\n<p>The event kicks off tomorrow at <strong>10 AM PT\/1 PM ET<\/strong>. We\u2019ll see you there.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/apple-march-2022-event\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/apple-march-2022-event-banner1.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about the Apple March 2022 event on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The thing about these virtual events is they\u2019ve really got a way of sneaking up on you. SE","slug":"iphone-se","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/447165759"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=447165759"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=447165759"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=447165759"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=447165759"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":115000,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/macbook\/","name":"macbook","slug":"macbook","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/115000"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=115000"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=115000"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=115000"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=115000"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":4109083,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/macbook-air\/","name":"macbook air","slug":"macbook-air","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/4109083"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=4109083"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=4109083"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=4109083"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=4109083"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2279665,"date":"2022-03-07T11:07:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-07T19:07:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2279665"},"modified":"2022-03-07T11:51:20","modified_gmt":"2022-03-07T19:51:20","slug":"robotics-founders-build-your-pitch-deck-around-problem-solving-not-technology","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/robotics-founders-build-your-pitch-deck-around-problem-solving-not-technology\/","title":{"rendered":"Robotics founders: Build your pitch deck around problem-solving, not technology"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">In robotics, the<\/span> remarkable often feels at odds with the practical. The Cassie robot captured the internet\u2019s imagination (<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2017\/02\/09\/cassie-the-ostrich-bot-does-the-bipedal-robot-chicken-walk\/\">ours included<\/a>) when it debuted in 2017 through a series of Oregon State University YouTube videos. It was one of the most exciting examples of robotics engineering since Boston Dynamics first made the scene.<\/p>\n<p>Commercial applications, however, are a different conversation entirely. In a world of purpose-built systems, it\u2019s not the first thing you see when you gaze upon the skinny legs of the ostrich-inspired bipedal \u2018bot. When Agility Robotics first spun out of OSU\u2019s College of Engineering, Cassie was being produced for research facilities. It\u2019s a worthy mission, but not exactly a cash cow.<\/p>\n<p>In a recent episode of TechCrunch Live, Agility&#8217;s co-founder and CTO, Jonathan Hurst, and Playground Global&#8217;s founding partner, Bruce Leak, joined us to discuss the robotic company&#8217;s journey from the lab to the commercial sector \u2014 and the role a good VC firm can play in that journey. The conversation spanned 30 minutes and includes a look at Agility Robotics&#8217; early pitch deck. The deck and video are embedded below.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cIf you\u2019re building a company that\u2019s building something that is really new and different, where are you going to hire engineers with experience with highly dynamic physical interaction, in the world, with force-sensitive behavior?\u201d asks Hurst. \u201cIt\u2019s just not common. Having students using the robots and a whole pipeline of people not only helps us, but it helps the whole infrastructure.\u201d<\/p>\n<h2>From lab to launch<\/h2>\n<p>Playground Global, an early-stage investment firm based in Palo Alto, discovered the robot the way most of us did \u2013 watching cool videos online.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cWe were surfing the internet like any good venture capital group, and we ran across the video that Agility released,\u201d says Leak. \u201cWe were super impressed. This product, at some level, was just an incredible pair of legs. But it could walk for hours and even run across uneven terrain in a very practical way. Seeing something like that, which we thought might not even be possible, we knew we had to meet the Agility team.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>Agility\u2019s seed\/Series A pitch deck wasn\u2019t focused on things like addressable market, and its insights into the robots\u2019 practical commercial applications were cursory. What it did, however, was break down the startup\u2019s impressive technologies. Hurst points to a tone shift between the presentation\u2019s first slide, reading \u201cDynamic robots for human environments,\u201d and its penultimate, \u201cMade for work.\u201d<\/p>\n<p><div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"><\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>In a recent episode of TechCrunch Live, Agility&#8217;s Jonathan Hurst and Playground Global&#8217;s Bruce Leak joined us to discuss the robotic company&#8217;s journey from the lab to the commercial is broken, Gecko is using robotics to help fix it"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Gecko Robotics\u2019 mission statement is \u201cTo protect today\u2019s critical infrastructure, and give form to tomorrow\u2019s.&#8221; It\u2019s certainly the sort of thing that rings true in the startup\u2019s home town of Pittsburgh, where the Fern Hollow Bridge collapsed under the weight of five vehicles in late-January, the day President Biden was visiting to talk infrastructure.<\/p>\n<p>Gecko\u2019s combination of robotics and software solutions is designed to discover cracks and other problem areas before they become much bigger problems. Specifically, the company\u2019s tech is designed to inspect industrial manufacturing structures for things like oil and gas, power, manufacturing and defense. That includes everything from pipelines to ships and tanks.<\/p>\n<p>This week, it announced <a href=\"https:\/\/blog.geckorobotics.com\/en\/press_and_news\/73-million-series-c-funding-will-bring-infrastructure-into-the-21st-century\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a $73 million raise<\/a> designed to accelerate its technology development and deployment. The round was led by XN LP and features Founders Fund, Drive Capital, Snowpoint Ventures, Joe Lonsdale, Mark Cuban and Gokul Rajaram. It brings the company\u2019s total funding to around $122 million, following a $40 million round, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/12\/16\/robotic-safety-inspectors-net-gecko-robotics-40-million\/\">back in 2019<\/a>.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2280377\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span class=\"embed-youtube embed breakout embed--video\" style=\"text-align:center; display: block;\"><iframe class=\"youtube-player\" width=\"640\" height=\"360\" src=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/embed\/bdeUbFv78dM?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent\" allowfullscreen=\"true\" style=\"border:0;\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation\"><\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Gecko&#8217;s unique combination of robotics, software, and AI radically improves the ability to inspect, protect, and efficiently maintain critical infrastructure,\u201d says XN partner, Tim Brown, in a release. \u201cWe are excited to partner with Jake and Troy as they extend Gecko&#8217;s powerful technology into new geographies and industries, helping customers collect and make sense of physical data to optimize the safety and performance of their assets.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The tech certainly ticks off the dirty and dangerous boxes of automation. It\u2019s designed to scale structures in extremely demanding and difficult settings. The robots spot damage that is often too subtle to be viewed with the human eye, and Gecko\u2019s software helps determine potential problem areas.<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Gecko Robotics\u2019 mission statement is \u201cTo protect today\u2019s critical infrastructure, and give form to tomorrow\u2019s.&#8221; It\u2019s certainly the sort of thing that rings true in the startup\u2019s home town of Pittsburgh, where the Fern Hollow Bridge collapsed under the weight of five vehicles in late-January, the day President Biden was visiting to talk infrastructure. staid MWC wraps up amid a lull in mobile excitement"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span class=\"featured__span-first-words\">I <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/25\/will-mobile-world-congress-be-more-of-the-same\/\">wrote a bit<\/span><\/a> last week about how it was going to be a weird MWC. By \u201cweird,\u201d I mean beyond the usual way that everything is weird all the time now. In addition to being the second time the show has been held during a global pandemic, the smartphone industry has undergone some big changes.<\/p>\n<p>Here\u2019s a quick bullet list from the last article:<\/p>\n<p>\u2022 People are upgrading their devices less frequently\/spending money elsewhere<br \/>\n\u2022 Supply chain issues and chip shortages aren\u2019t helping<br \/>\n\u2022 LG and HTC have stopped making phones and dramatically ramped down, respectively &#8212; though the latter is, very least<a href=\"https:\/\/www.digitimes.com\/news\/a20220302PD215.html\"> ready to jump<\/a> from one buzzword (blockchain) to another (metaverse)<br \/>\n\u2022 Huawei has been sidelined by sanctions<br \/>\n\u2022 Companies like Samsung and Apple now rely on their own events<br \/>\n\u2022 That, in turn, has opened the China market to Xiaomi and a ton of BBK companies<br \/>\n\u2022 Qualcomm has been unveiling its big Snapdragon chip, sending companies racing to have the first device with the tech<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2279734\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Most of these things feel like headwinds for an event that had become the de facto smartphone show. I\u2019d suggested that MWC seemed destined to return to its default state as a B2B\/network\/carrier show, and things seem to have largely played out that way in Barcelona this week.<\/p>\n<p>It\u2019s doesn\u2019t really bode well for the excitement level around what\u2019s ostensibly become a smartphone show when arguably the two biggest pieces of consumers news &#8212; the <a href=\"https:\/\/www.samsung.com\/us\/computing\/galaxy-book-pro\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Samsung Galaxy Book 2 Pro<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/28\/lenovos-new-thinkpad-kicks-off-qualcomms-new-snapdragon-laptop-platform\/\">Lenovo ThinkPad X13s<\/a> &#8212; are both laptops. Huawei also managed to make a bit of a splash with its own with a pair of #notphones, in the form of the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/28\/huawei-gets-into-the-e-reader-game-with-a-combo-note-taking-device\/\">MatePad Paper e-reader\/tablet<\/a> and MateBook X Pro #notaMacbook.<\/p>\n<p>Immediately following the show, I asked Huawei CTO Paul Scanlan some questions about the company\u2019s plans to right the ship following U.S. sanctions that have hobbled its consumer efforts by cutting off access to giants like Google and Qualcomm. His response:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>We try to differentiate by the other things we do, which are power management, batteries, and some software at the HarmonyOS layer. We\u2019ve also tried to differentiate Harmony from things like an Apple or Google ecosystem by presenting it as something connects across industry components \u2013 connected treadmill, connected, bike, connected TV, connected speakers, connected air conditioners, connected heart rate monitors.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>[\u2026]In China itself, the marketshare is good still. In terms of overseas market, where maybe you need the differentiated capability of GMS (Google Mobile Services) or iOS ecosystems, obviously that\u2019s tricky for us. That\u2019s why we\u2019ve extended the consumer business group to include a lot of other different devices, not just smartphones. We took <a href=\"https:\/\/www.scmp.com\/tech\/tech-war\/article\/3150036\/huawei-says-us-sanctions-cause-us30-billion-loss-its-handset-revenue\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a $30 billionish hit<\/a> over the year for the smartphones.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The company declined to comment on its place in the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/25\/mwc-2022-limits-russia\/\">Russian market<\/a> following the recent invasion of Ukraine.<\/p>\n<p>A number of other key Chinese manufacturers led the way in the actual device announcements. TCL added a bunch of models to its 30 line, including the TCL 30 5G &#8212; the only model of the bunch to support the aforementioned wireless technology. The company also showed off a new foldable that\u2019s very much still in the concept stage. Former Huawei brand Honor showed off its 6.8-inch flagship, the Magic4, while former-Xiaomi brand Poco debuted the 6.7-inch X4 Pro 5G. OnePlus, for its part, offered additional details around the 10 Pro device it unveiled back at CES.<\/p>\n<p>You\u2019d be forgiven if you missed any of this earth-shattering news over the past week.<\/p>\n<p>For my money, the most exciting smartphone news of the week happened outside of the show. We\u2019re about to see the entry of two brand new players in the category, both with solid pedigrees. For reasons I went into above, this current moment is both an extremely challenging and potentially rewarding time to enter the space. The category is well established, but who knows, maybe people are waiting for a new player to shake things up?<\/p>\n<p>First off is Nothing. The hardware startup is getting ready to follow in the footsteps of founder Carl Pei\u2019s first company, OnePlus, with the launch of a new handset. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/02\/nothing-smartphone-carl-pei\/?tpcc=tcplustwitter\">A source told TechCrunch<\/a> that Nothing is planning to announce its first phone by next month. The device was shown off in the back rooms of the Barcelona show. We know it will feature transparent elements in line with the company\u2019s first product, Ear(1), but beyond that, things get hazy.<\/p>\n<p>OSOM, which rose from the ashes of Essential\u2019s spectacular implosion, meanwhile, was initially planning to use MWC as a launchpad for its first device, the OV1. Ultimately, however, Qualcomm made the company an offer it couldn\u2019t refuse, so <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/03\/osom-talks-its-first-phone-ahead-of-a-q4-release\/\">the firm pushed the device\u2019s release back<\/a> from Q3 to Q4.<\/p>\n<p>\u201cThey love that we\u2019re local. We have a longstanding history with the team of working directly with them,\u201d founder and CEO Jason Keats told TechCrunch. \u201cOne of our partners is big enough that Qualcomm was like, \u2018holy crap, you\u2019re working with them? We want to be more involved with what you\u2019re doing, as well.\u2019 They came back and said OSOM has the opportunity to do something new, exciting. To change how all of this works. And I think, part of it is we aren\u2019t a huge company, so if their yields aren\u2019t gigantic, they don\u2019t need to worry about shipping me five million chips in a month.\u201d<\/p>\n<p>The company also offered up some specs to tide us over, and showed off a clever USB-C connector with a switch that makes it possible to toggle between data transfer and just straight up charging. It\u2019s one of those things I\u2019m frankly surprised more companies haven\u2019t tried.<\/p>\n<p>I\u2019m not giving up on MWC as the premier smartphone show just yet, though things largely played out as we expected. It was another weird year full of unique challenges for the industry and the world at large. Whatever remains of people\u2019s attention spans is understandably elsewhere right now.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/mwc-2022\/\"><img src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/02\/mwc-2022-banner.jpg\" alt=\"Read more about MWC 2022 on TechCrunch\" \/><\/a><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>I wrote a bit last week about how it was going to be a weird MWC. By \u201cweird,\u201d I mean beyond the usual way that everything is weird all the time now. In addition to being the second time the show has been held during a global pandemic, the smartphone industry has undergone some big
